## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: materials science & solid mechanics (thermomechanical constitutive modeling)
**Analysis**: With sigma as stress, epsilon as strain, and T as temperature, this is a classic constitutive-law identification problem in continuum/solid mechanics where temperature affects elastic modulus, thermal strain, yield/flow stress, and strain-hardening behavior.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke’s law (isothermal linear elasticity): sigma = c0 * epsilon (small-strain elastic regime)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (linear-in-T): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (elastic stiffness changes with temperature)
- Thermoelastic strain shift: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * T) (thermal expansion reduces/measures mechanical strain)
- General thermoelastic coupling: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * (epsilon - c2 * T) (both modulus and thermal strain depend on T)
- Nonlinear elastic polynomial: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (moderate strains, empirical hyperelastic fit)
- Ludwik/Hollomon-type hardening (stress–strain power law): sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (plastic hardening beyond yield, no strain-rate term)
- Voce-type exponential hardening (approach to saturation): sigma = c0 + c1 * (1 - exp(-c2 * epsilon)) (strain hardening that asymptotes)
- Logarithmic hardening: sigma = c0 + c1 * log(c2 * epsilon + 1) (materials showing diminishing hardening rate)
- Thermal softening as exponential factor: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * exp(-c3 * T) (flow stress decreases with T)
- Thermal softening as power factor: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 - c4 * T)**c5 (empirical softening over limited T range)
- Smooth elastic-to-plastic transition (tanh blend): sigma = (c0 * epsilon) + (c1 * epsilon**c2) * (0.5 + 0.5 * tanh(c3 * (epsilon - c4))) (gradual yielding/transition without a sharp piecewise law)
- Entropic/rubber-like elasticity (if epsilon interpreted as stretch): sigma = c0 * T * (epsilon - c1 / (epsilon**2)) (temperature-proportional network stress, large-deformation elastomers)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Elastic stiffness decreasing with temperature often appears as a multiplicative modulus factor on epsilon, e.g., (c0 + c1*T)*epsilon or exp(-c*T)*epsilon.
- Thermal expansion enters as an effective strain offset, commonly epsilon - c*T, implying sigma goes to ~0 when epsilon ≈ c*T (free expansion).
- Plastic hardening commonly follows power-law in strain, so epsilon**n terms (or sums of powers) are strong candidates when sigma grows superlinearly with epsilon.
- Saturating hardening (approach to a limiting stress) is well-captured by 1 - exp(-c*epsilon) forms multiplied by a scale, producing an asymptote at large epsilon.
- Diminishing returns in hardening can also manifest as log(c*epsilon + 1), giving rapid initial increase then slower growth.
- Thermal softening frequently acts multiplicatively on the entire stress response (elastic + plastic), suggesting sigma = g(epsilon) * h(T) rather than purely additive T terms.
- Yield/transition regions are often best represented by smooth blending functions like tanh(c*(epsilon-c0)) multiplying a plastic term, avoiding discontinuous piecewise fits.
- If sigma scales approximately linearly with T at fixed deformation (common in entropic elasticity), structures like T * f(epsilon) become plausible.
